This Horror Show Shows Who We Are A student of mine told me about a new show called â€œSquid Game.â€ It is a South Korean â€œthriller series,â€ as they call it, which has become a pop culture phenomenon and is the no. 1 show in more than 90 countries. The show presents several hundred people who are all in great financial debt and in dire emotional states. The producers pit them against each other, even if they are very close, and make them hate each other. The winner takes millions of dollars, and the others are killed. This show wouldnâ€™t be so horrifying if it didnâ€™t portray our true nature. The very fact that we watch such a show enthusiastically is proof that underneath the â€œcivilizedâ€ faÃ§ade, our nature is as the show depicts. It works like a magnet. We love to watch the struggle between good and evil, as long as we are safe from the consequences of the battle. The thing is that in this show, there is no good; there is only evil.  Indeed, humans are the worst being in reality. What makes us so uniquely evil is the fact that we explicitly want to harm others. We do not want to eat others because we will starve unless we do so; we want to see them suffer! We derive pleasure from othersâ€™ pain, and derive the most pleasure when we are the ones inflicting it. We often say that reality is like a jungle, where the strong eat the weak. However, in the jungle, the strong do not want to destroy the weak; they want to eat. Once they are full, they want to sleep and play, and not kill or hurt for fun. In the human jungle, we do not want to eat other people; we want to see them hurting! This is why the natural jungle thrives without any laws while the human jungle, which we mistakenly refer to as â€œcivilization,â€ is disintegrating despite the laws that strive to limit our barbarity. If we had any hopes of finding goodness in human nature, â€œSquid Game,â€ and mainly its popularity, proves that we have nothing to hope for when it comes to human nature. If we can create such shows, and if they can be so popular, then we can do such horrors in real life. The only possible good that can come out of such a show is the realization that it is not fantasy, but an authentic depiction of who we are. Maybe if we realize this, we will be willing to do something about changing ourselves. The current trend is to dull our awareness of the human horror show we live in by making cannabis available and legal. Indeed, the more we learn about human nature, the more we realize that perhaps it is better to numb ourselves through life until itâ€™s over. For now, weâ€™re cheering at the sight of other people suffering, much like people used to cheer at the sight of poor men fighting against lions in ancient Rome. Only if we realize that it is not okay to be like that, our minds might open to other options. If such a diabolical program can be the no. 1 show in more than 90 countries, it means that the entire world is immersed in unhinged viciousness. There is a solution, but it is demanding and must encompass the entire world if it is to succeed. To change who we are, we must initiate a worldwide educational process where such programs are forbidden and pro-human-connection programs are produced and aired. Even if they are not popular, at first, we cannot allow ourselves to be exposed to the violent poison and culture of narcissism that we consume today. They may be sweet, but they are lethal. If people donâ€™t want to watch shows about human connection, they can put aside their media devices and simply talk to one another. This will already be a major improvement to the current situation. It may not sound like fun, but what is the option? To live out the â€œSquid Game.â€ Besides, after some practice, we will discover that connection and care are far more rewarding and pleasant than destruction and cruelty, and do not carry the negative side effect that is our current culture.

This Horror Show Shows Who We Are A student of mine told me about a new show called â€œSquid Game.â€ It is a South Korean â€œthriller series,â€ as they call it, which has become a pop culture phenomenon and is the no. 1 show in more than 90 countries. The show presents several hundred people who are all in great financial debt and in dire emotional states. The producers pit them against each other, even if they are very close, and make them hate each other. The winner takes millions of dollars, and the others are killed. This show wouldnâ€™t be so horrifying if it didnâ€™t portray our true nature. The very fact that we watch such a show enthusiastically is proof that underneath the â€œcivilizedâ€ faÃ§ade, our nature is as the show depicts. It works like a magnet. We love to watch the struggle between good and evil, as long as we are safe from the consequences of the battle. The thing is that in this show, there is no good; there is only evil.  Indeed, humans are the worst being in reality. What makes us so uniquely evil is the fact that we explicitly want to harm others. We do not want to eat others because we will starve unless we do so; we want to see them suffer! We derive pleasure from othersâ€™ pain, and derive the most pleasure when we are the ones inflicting it. We often say that reality is like a jungle, where the strong eat the weak. However, in the jungle, the strong do not want to destroy the weak; they want to eat. Once they are full, they want to sleep and play, and not kill or hurt for fun. In the human jungle, we do not want to eat other people; we want to see them hurting! This is why the natural jungle thrives without any laws while the human jungle, which we mistakenly refer to as â€œcivilization,â€ is disintegrating despite the laws that strive to limit our barbarity. If we had any hopes of finding goodness in human nature, â€œSquid Game,â€ and mainly its popularity, proves that we have nothing to hope for when it comes to human nature. If we can create such shows, and if they can be so popular, then we can do such horrors in real life. The only possible good that can come out of such a show is the realization that it is not fantasy, but an authentic depiction of who we are. Maybe if we realize this, we will be willing to do something about changing ourselves. The current trend is to dull our awareness of the human horror show we live in by making cannabis available and legal. Indeed, the more we learn about human nature, the more we realize that perhaps it is better to numb ourselves through life until itâ€™s over. For now, weâ€™re cheering at the sight of other people suffering, much like people used to cheer at the sight of poor men fighting against lions in ancient Rome. Only if we realize that it is not okay to be like that, our minds might open to other options. If such a diabolical program can be the no. 1 show in more than 90 countries, it means that the entire world is immersed in unhinged viciousness. There is a solution, but it is demanding and must encompass the entire world if it is to succeed. To change who we are, we must initiate a worldwide educational process where such programs are forbidden and pro-human-connection programs are produced and aired. Even if they are not popular, at first, we cannot allow ourselves to be exposed to the violent poison and culture of narcissism that we consume today. They may be sweet, but they are lethal. If people donâ€™t want to watch shows about human connection, they can put aside their media devices and simply talk to one another. This will already be a major improvement to the current situation. It may not sound like fun, but what is the option? To live out the â€œSquid Game.â€ Besides, after some practice, we will discover that connection and care are far more rewarding and pleasant than destruction and cruelty, and do not carry the negative side effect that is our current culture.

Nice to see asian media getting more global recognition. The storytelling, originality and lack of creative restraints (pc culture bs) leads to far superior media content.  We have overly polished, tacky, generic shows and movies littered with agenda political or otherwise. They see storytelling as an art form and whether its a real life show/movie or an anime series that is the artwork.  In this age of political correctness and pandering around touchy subject matter people may be more aware of the feelings of others but creativity and self expression has really taken a hit.   I miss series and movies that delved into the taboo subjects and unfiltered comedy. No subject should be too offensive or non confirmative especially in the fields of fictional media and comedy as they are there to explore society and its issues or to extrapolate from personal experience and opinion.   Comedy itself takes a look at society and mocks nonsensical rules, behaviour or other occurrences. This turns real life issues and subjects into humour helping to normalise and de-stigmatise, bringing people from different backgrounds (race, gender, ethnicity, religion ect) closer together. By fostering understanding and allowing people with little in common to share a laugh over some of the issues, stereotypes, interactions or more heavy subject matter we can both have a laugh and forget about our worries and realise we have more in common than perhaps we first thought.

I can almost relate to how the show attracted very different views. It looks like my native town's guys were far detached from the rest of the world. HK audience likes to pick a lot of "bugs" in the show like they would scrutinize Doraemon stories full of logical flaws and errors/anachronisms and so on. I think Jung most likely DOES have a lot of role in the show, but she has mixed reviews among HK viewers, and for very cultural reasons Lee (the other character) gets far more attention in hk than among other viewers.  My fair judgment is the show sells really well, and the mainstream viewers don't actually care about the countless "logical flaws" you could pick. Those flaws, you know, are likely "how is this guy not dead", "this is impossible to do in real life", "it defies logic/gravity", and so on. That's just jealousy talking.  Something haters want to believe.    My cousin operates one of Seoul's largest plastic surgery hospitals and according to him, that's completely false.  This rumour started in the 80's when it gained some popularity but these days, most of his clients are foreigners; especially asians wanting to look like Korean celebrities or "more Korean".    He says plastic surgery is not all about gaining beauty.  He sees Korean patients more for medical reasons; reconstructive surgery due to accidents or birth defects.    These days Koreans are more focused on skin and hair care--or improvements to accentuate their natural traits.  Koreans are also very health conscious, eat well, exercise, avoid stress and be happy.   Part of his practice is to discourage people from cosmetic surgery.  They have therapists on staff and suggest skincare to start with.  Good skin has a huge effect on the overall look of a person.    Those that you might see on the streets shopping with bandaged faces are definitely NOT Koreans.  These are surgery tourists, here in Seoul to get work done and shop like mad.     Apparently, no amount of plastic surgery is going to take you from "unattractive" to "gorgeous".  There has to be a certain amount of basics.    Unlike what most people perceive to be physical "beauty", this actually comes from within.  No cliche.  He adds, the reason why these actors seem attractive is mostly due to their presentation; that is smile and laugh a lot, fashionable, relaxed, and confidence without arrogance.   Of all the asians,   Koreans tend to have a softer appearance and demeanour.    Lastly, from the screen, he can tell that non of these actors have had work done.  The faces of people with plastic surgery move differently to the trained eye.  He says, the two older men might of had botox or fillers but no surgery.  Anyways, with so much online, these people have their entire lives on display.  Koreans would know if they've had work done.  Some are even very open about it.  And for celebrities, whether Korean or not, appearance is part of their job.   So stop the nonsensical hate.

Dalgona and ppopki are all from the forgotten tradition of Japan called Katanugi. The right-handed umbrella on the candy is only used in Japanese signage.  Katanugi was forgotten due to the possible fire scars which will last forever in a child's life. Boiling Sugar and Baking Soda together is very hazardous.  https://youtu.be/YmwGyAQtJTY <- RARE modernized and industrialized Katanugi video. Most of them are made at the factories for safety.  South Koreans are adding Saccharin for further enhancing sweetness of Ppopki now in Seoul, South Korea. You could find the recipe videos of Korean uploaders showing 'New Sugar' in the list of the ingredients. New Sugar is the product name of the white powder mixture of Glucose and Saccharin. Most of the South Korean foods are full of artificial additives for the bad quality of South Korean agricultural products and no cold chain. The adoption rate of cold chain is similar to that of Thailand in South Korea.

You should know exactly the "Red light, Green light" game from "The Squid Game". The rules for playing this game in Korea are as follows. 1. One blindfolded shouting "Red Light". 2. At that time, all but tagger moved to the tagger at once. 3. When the tagger shouts "Green light" . When the tagger looks at people, the person who moves is drawn towards the tagger and holds it with the little finger. 4. As everyone slowly approaches towards the tagger, he shakes the hand between the hostage and the tag and runs away again as a starting line. 5. Tagger catches one of them. 6. The person caught becomes the tag in the next game.

The thing is - I loved everything about Squid Game, it was great from the beginning till the end and the cast was chosen perfectly, but if this is the first Korean drama you've watched, then I must enlighten you that South Korea makes great dramas in general. The romance ones may seem restrained and definitely less explicit (sex scenes are rare), but when it comes to thriller, crime and mystery ones, Kdramas are in my opinion the best. Unfortunately, only recently they've started adding shows on Netflix, mostly the new ones, but there are other streaming sites where you can watch them with subtitles, such as Viki. On Netflix my favorite ones are Flower of Evil (though it's unavailable in my country now) and Kingdom. The Lies Within is good too.
